مَوَالِيَ حِلْفٍ لَا مَوَالِيَ قَرَابَةٍ وَلَكِنْ قَطِيناً يَعْصِرُونَ الصَّنَوْبَرَا فَأَمَّا مَا قَصَدَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِقَوْلِهِ: «مَنْ كُنْتُ مَوْلَاهُ، فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ» فَإِنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ أَمْرَيْنِ أَحَدُهُمَا مَنْ كُنْتُ نَاصِرَهُ عَلَى دِينِهِ وَحَامِياً عَنْهُ بِظَاهِرِي وَبَاطِنِي وَسِرِّي وَعَلَانِيَتِي فَعَلِيٌّ نَاصِرُهُ عَلَى هَذَا السَّبِيلِ فَتَكُونُ فَائِدَةُ ذَلِكَ الْإِخْبَارُ عَنْ أَنَّ بَاطِنَ عَلِيٍّ وَظَاهِرَهُ فِي نُصْرَةِ الدِّينِ وَالْمُؤْمِنِينَ سَوَاءٌ وَالْقَطْعَ عَلَى سَرِيرَتِهِ وَعُلُوِّ رُتْبَتِهِ ; وَلَيْسَ يُعْتَقَدُ ذَلِكَ فِي كُلِّ نَاصِرٍ لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ بِظَاهِرِهِ ; لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَنْصُرُ النَّاصِرُ بِظَاهِرِهِ طَلَبَ النِّفَاقِ وَالسُّمْعَةِ وَابْتِغَاءَ الرِّفْدِ وَمَتَاعِ الدُّنْيَا فَإِذَا أَخْبَرَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَّ نُصْرَةَ بَعْضِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي الدِّينِ وَالْمُسْلِمِينَ كَنُصْرَتِهِ هُوَ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قُطِعَ عَلَى طَهَارَةِ سَرِيرَتِهِ وَسَلَامَةِ بَاطِنِهِ وَهَذِهِ فَضِيلَةٌ عَظِيمَةٌ. وَيَحْتَمِلُ أَيْضاً أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُرَادُ بِقَوْلِهِ : «فَمَنْ كُنْتُ مَوْلَاهُ فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ»، أَيْ مَنْ كُنْتُ مَحْبُوباً عِنْدَهُ وَوَلِيّاً لَهُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِي وَبَاطِنِي فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ أَيْ إِنَّ وِلَاءَهُ وَمَحَبَّتَهُ مِنْ ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَاجِبٌ كَمَا أَنَّ وِلَائِي وَمَحَبَّتِي عَلَى هَذَا السَّبِيلِ وَاجِبٌ فَيَكُونُ قَدْ أَوْجَبَ مُوَالَاتَهُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَلَسْنَا نُوَالِي كُلَّ مَنْ ظَهَرَ مِنْهُ الْإِيمَانُ عَلَى هَذِهِ السَّبِيلِ بَلْ إِنَّمَا نُوَالِيهِمْ فِي الظَّاهِرِ دُونَ الْبَاطِنِ .
فَإِنْ قِيلَ : فَمَا وَجْهُ تَخْصِيصِهِ بِهَذَا الْقَوْلِ وَقَدْ كَانَ عِنْدَكُمْ فِي الصَّحَابَةِ خَلْقٌ عَظِيمٌ ظَاهِرُهُمْ كَبَاطِنِهِمْ؟ قِيلَ لَهُ : يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ بَلَغَهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَدْحُ قَادِحٍ فِيهِ أَوْ ثَلْبُ ثَالِبٍ أَوْ أَخْبَرَ أَنَّ قَوْماً مِنْ أَهْلِ النِّفَاقِ وَالشُّرَاةِ سَيَطْعَنُونَ عَلَيْهِ وَيَزْعُمُونَ أَنَّهُ فَارَقَ الدِّينَ وَحَكَمَ فِي أَمْرِ اللهِ تَعَالَى الْآدَمِيِّينَ وَيُسْقِطُونَ بِذَلِكَ وِلَايَتَهُ وَيُزِيلُونَ وَلَاءَهُ فَقَالَ ذَلِكَ فِيهِ لِيَنْفِيَ ذَلِكَ عَنْهُ فِي وَقْتِهِ وَبَعْدِهِ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى لَوْ عَلِمَ أَنَّ عَلِيّاً سَيُفَارِقُ الدِّينَ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ أَوْ غَيْرِهِ عَلَى مَا قُرِفَ بِهِ لَمْ يَأْمُرْ نَبِيَّهُ أَنْ يَأْمُرَ النَّاسَ بِاعْتِقَادِ وِلَايَاتِهِ وَمَحَبَّتِهِ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَالْقَطْعِ عَلَى طَهَارَتِهِ وَهُوَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ يَخْتِمُ عَمَلَهُ بِمُفَارَقَةِ الدِّينِ لِأَنَّ مَنْ هَذِهِ سَبِيلُهُ فِي مَعْلُومِ اللهِ تَعَالَى فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَطُّ وَلِيّاً لِلَّهِ وَلَا مِمَّنْ يَسْتَحِقُّ الْوِلَايَةَ وَالْمَحَبَّةَ، وَفِي أَمْرِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِمُوَالَاةِ عَلِيٍّ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى سُقُوطِ مَا قَرَفَهُ أَهْلُ النِّفَاقِ وَالضَّلَالِ بِهِ .
فَإِنْ قَالُوا : فَإِذَا كَانَ هَذَا هُوَ الَّذِي أَرَادَهُ فَلِمَ لَمْ يَقُلْ : عَلِيٌّ مُؤْمِنُ الظَّاهِرِ وَالْبَاطِنِ نَقِيُّ السَّرِيرَةِ وَخَاتِمُ لِعَمَلِهِ بِالْبِرِّ وَالطَّاعَةِ فَيُزِيلُ الْإِشْكَالَ؟ قِيلَ لَهُمْ : لَيْسَ لَنَا الِاعْتِرَاضُ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي تَخَيُّرِ الْأَلْفَاظِ وَلَعَلَّهُ أُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِ أَنَّ إِذَاعَةَ هَذَا الْكَلَامِ وَجَمْعَ النَّاسِ لَهُ وَتَقْدِيمَ التَّقْرِيرِ لِوُجُوبِ طَاعَتِهِ لُطْفٌ لِعَلِيٍّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَأَنَّهُ أَجْمَعُ لِلْقُلُوبِ عَلَى مَحَبَّتِهِ وَمُوَالَاتِهِ فَلَا سُؤَالَ عَلَيْنَا فِي ذَلِكَ .
ثُمَّ يُقَالُ لَهُمْ : فَلَوْ كَانَ الرَّسُولُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِنَّمَا أَرَادَ بِهَذَا الْقَوْلِ النَّصَّ عَلَيْهِ فَلِمَ لَمْ يَقُلْ : هَذَا إِمَامُكُمْ بَعْدِي الْوَاجِبَةُ طَاعَتُهُ فَاسْمَعُوا لَهُ وَأَطِيعُوا فَيُزِيلُ الْوَهْمَ وَالْإِشْكَالَ ؟ فَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ أَجَابُوا بِهِ، فَهُوَ جَوَابٌ لَهُمْ فِيمَا سَأَلُوا عَنْهُ .
Clients of alliance, not clients of kinship, but dependents who press pine nuts. As for what the Prophet (peace be upon him) intended by his statement: 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla,' it can bear two meanings: one of them is: whoever I am his supporter in his religion and his defender, in my apparent and hidden, secret and public, then Ali is his supporter in this way; so the benefit of that is the informing that Ali's hidden and apparent are equal in supporting the religion and the believers, and certainty about his inner state and high rank. And that is not believed about every apparent supporter of the believers, because the supporter may support with his apparent seeking hypocrisy and reputation and seeking reward and worldly goods. So when the Prophet (peace be upon him) informed that the support of some of the believers in the religion and the Muslims is like his own support (peace be upon him), certainty is made about the purity of his inner state and soundness of his hidden, and this is a great virtue. And it is also possible that the intended meaning of his statement: 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla' is: whoever I am beloved to him and a friend to him in my apparent and hidden, then Ali is his mawla, meaning that his friendship and love in his apparent and hidden are obligatory just as my friendship and love in this way are obligatory. So he has made obligatory his friendship in his apparent and hidden, and we do not befriend everyone who manifests faith in this way, but rather we befriend them in apparent only, not in hidden. If it is said: What is the reason for singling him out with this statement when among you there were many Companions whose apparent was like their hidden? It is said to him: It is possible that it reached him (peace be upon him) a disparagement of a disparager or a slander of a slanderer, or he was informed that a group from the people of hypocrisy and the Kharijites would attack him and claim that he had left the religion and judged in God's matter concerning humans, and thereby they would nullify his friendship and remove his loyalty. So he said that concerning him to negate that from him in his time and after, because if God knew that Ali would leave the religion by arbitration or otherwise according to what he was accused of, He would not have commanded His Prophet to command people to believe in his friendship and love in his apparent and hidden and to be certain of his purity, while He knew that he would end his life by leaving the religion. For whoever is such in God's knowledge, he was never a friend of God nor among those who deserve friendship and love. And in the command of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) to befriend Ali in his apparent and hidden is evidence of the fall of what the people of hypocrisy and misguidance accused him of. Then they said: If this is what he intended, why did he not say: 'Ali is a believer in apparent and hidden, pure of inner state, and his work ends with piety and obedience' to remove ambiguity? It was said to them: We have no objection to the Prophet (peace be upon him) in choosing words; perhaps it was revealed to him that publicizing this speech, gathering people for it, and presenting the affirmation of the obligation of obedience to him was a kindness for Ali (peace be upon him) and that it is more gathering of hearts for his love and friendship. So there is no question upon us in that. Then it is said to them: If the Messenger (peace be upon him) intended by this statement explicit appointment of him, why did he not say: 'This is your imam after me, obedience to whom is obligatory, so listen to him and obey' to remove doubt and ambiguity? Whatever they answer with, it is an answer for them regarding what they asked about.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a response to a Shiite claim that the Prophet's statement 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla' constitutes explicit appointment (nass) of Ali as successor. The author, Imam al-Baqillani, begins by quoting a line of poetry that distinguishes between two types of mawla: by alliance (hulf) and by kinship. This sets the stage that the word 'mawla' can have multiple meanings. He then states that the Prophet's statement can bear two meanings. First, 'mawla' means supporter or helper (nasir). In this interpretation, the Prophet is informing that Ali's hidden and apparent support for the religion is equal to his own, a great virtue, but not every apparent supporter is like that because some support for show. Second, 'mawla' means beloved and friend (mahbub wali). In this interpretation, the Prophet is obligating love and friendship for Ali both outwardly and inwardly, just as the Prophet himself is to be loved. This does not mean political succession. Then an objection is raised: Why single out Ali when many Companions were sincerely faithful? The answer is that the Prophet foresaw that hypocrites and Kharijites would slander Ali, claiming he left the religion, so this statement was to refute that slander in advance. God would not command belief in Ali's friendship if He knew Ali would apostatize. Thus the statement proves the falsehood of the accusations. A further objection: Why didn't the Prophet say explicitly 'Ali is a believer inside and out' to avoid confusion? The answer: We do not object to the Prophet's choice of words; God perhaps inspired this phrasing to gather people's hearts to love Ali. Another objection: If the Prophet intended appointment, why not say 'This is your imam after me'? The author then turns the argument, saying that any response the opponents give to that question can also be applied to their own objection. This is a classic kalam rhetorical move to show inconsistency in the opponent's position.

Key Terms
مولاه (mawla)
نصرة (support)
محبة (love)
ولاية (wila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'mawla' in the hadith can only mean 'master' or 'successor', thus the hadith is an explicit appointment of Ali as caliph.
Correction: Baqillani shows that 'mawla' can mean 'supporter' or 'beloved friend', as attested by Arabic usage, and these interpretations are contextually valid.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what are the two possible meanings of 'mawla' in the Prophet's statement?
A) Successor and leader
B) Supporter and beloved/friend
C) Master and guardian
D) Father and brother

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that the hadith can be understood as referring to support or love, not necessarily succession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani teaches that true support of the religion must come from both the inner and outer self. Are you supporting Islam only with your outward actions, or is your heart truly aligned? What is one area where your inner state does not match your outward display?
?
The Prophet declared that Ali's hidden and apparent are equal in supporting the faith. If your hidden self were revealed, would it match your apparent devotion? What would you need to change to close that gap?
?
The lesson says we do not befriend every believer with full inner love. Is there a believer—perhaps from a different sect or background—whom you refuse to love inwardly? How does this lesson challenge you to examine that barrier?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
Why Single Out Ali? Baqillani's Response to an Objection
Baqillani answers the objection about singling out Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani responds to the objection that the Prophet's statement about Ali seems to single him out for praise when many Companions were equally sincere, and how he argues it was a refutation of future slander.

Core Idea
The Prophet foresaw slander against Ali, so his statement was a defense, not an appointment.

After explaining the two meanings, Baqillani anticipates an objection: Why did the Prophet single out Ali in this way when there were many virtuous Companions? His answer is that the Prophet was preemptively refuting accusations that would be made by hypocrites and Kharijites, claiming that Ali had left the religion. This lesson examines that insightful response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objector asks: If the hadith is about virtue, why was Ali singled out when many Companions were equally sincere? Understand the force of this question.
This objection assumes that the hadith is praising Ali, but the opponent may use it to argue for his special status.
2
Study Baqillani's answer
Baqillani says the Prophet was informed that people would slander Ali, claiming he left the religion. The statement was to negate that slander in advance and to affirm Ali's sincerity.
This answer does not claim that the hadith is about political succession.
3
Consider the deeper argument
Baqillani adds that God would not have commanded people to believe in Ali's friendship if He knew Ali would apostatize. This reinforces the point that the hadith proves Ali's righteousness.
This is a theological argument about divine knowledge and the impossibility of God commanding something false.

مَوَالِيَ حِلْفٍ لَا مَوَالِيَ قَرَابَةٍ وَلَكِنْ قَطِيناً يَعْصِرُونَ الصَّنَوْبَرَا فَأَمَّا مَا قَصَدَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِقَوْلِهِ: «مَنْ كُنْتُ مَوْلَاهُ، فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ» فَإِنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ أَمْرَيْنِ أَحَدُهُمَا مَنْ كُنْتُ نَاصِرَهُ عَلَى دِينِهِ وَحَامِياً عَنْهُ بِظَاهِرِي وَبَاطِنِي وَسِرِّي وَعَلَانِيَتِي فَعَلِيٌّ نَاصِرُهُ عَلَى هَذَا السَّبِيلِ فَتَكُونُ فَائِدَةُ ذَلِكَ الْإِخْبَارُ عَنْ أَنَّ بَاطِنَ عَلِيٍّ وَظَاهِرَهُ فِي نُصْرَةِ الدِّينِ وَالْمُؤْمِنِينَ سَوَاءٌ وَالْقَطْعَ عَلَى سَرِيرَتِهِ وَعُلُوِّ رُتْبَتِهِ ; وَلَيْسَ يُعْتَقَدُ ذَلِكَ فِي كُلِّ نَاصِرٍ لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ بِظَاهِرِهِ ; لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَنْصُرُ النَّاصِرُ بِظَاهِرِهِ طَلَبَ النِّفَاقِ وَالسُّمْعَةِ وَابْتِغَاءَ الرِّفْدِ وَمَتَاعِ الدُّنْيَا فَإِذَا أَخْبَرَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَّ نُصْرَةَ بَعْضِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي الدِّينِ وَالْمُسْلِمِينَ كَنُصْرَتِهِ هُوَ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قُطِعَ عَلَى طَهَارَةِ سَرِيرَتِهِ وَسَلَامَةِ بَاطِنِهِ وَهَذِهِ فَضِيلَةٌ عَظِيمَةٌ. وَيَحْتَمِلُ أَيْضاً أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُرَادُ بِقَوْلِهِ : «فَمَنْ كُنْتُ مَوْلَاهُ فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ»، أَيْ مَنْ كُنْتُ مَحْبُوباً عِنْدَهُ وَوَلِيّاً لَهُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِي وَبَاطِنِي فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ أَيْ إِنَّ وِلَاءَهُ وَمَحَبَّتَهُ مِنْ ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَاجِبٌ كَمَا أَنَّ وِلَائِي وَمَحَبَّتِي عَلَى هَذَا السَّبِيلِ وَاجِبٌ فَيَكُونُ قَدْ أَوْجَبَ مُوَالَاتَهُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَلَسْنَا نُوَالِي كُلَّ مَنْ ظَهَرَ مِنْهُ الْإِيمَانُ عَلَى هَذِهِ السَّبِيلِ بَلْ إِنَّمَا نُوَالِيهِمْ فِي الظَّاهِرِ دُونَ الْبَاطِنِ .
فَإِنْ قِيلَ : فَمَا وَجْهُ تَخْصِيصِهِ بِهَذَا الْقَوْلِ وَقَدْ كَانَ عِنْدَكُمْ فِي الصَّحَابَةِ خَلْقٌ عَظِيمٌ ظَاهِرُهُمْ كَبَاطِنِهِمْ؟ قِيلَ لَهُ : يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ بَلَغَهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَدْحُ قَادِحٍ فِيهِ أَوْ ثَلْبُ ثَالِبٍ أَوْ أَخْبَرَ أَنَّ قَوْماً مِنْ أَهْلِ النِّفَاقِ وَالشُّرَاةِ سَيَطْعَنُونَ عَلَيْهِ وَيَزْعُمُونَ أَنَّهُ فَارَقَ الدِّينَ وَحَكَمَ فِي أَمْرِ اللهِ تَعَالَى الْآدَمِيِّينَ وَيُسْقِطُونَ بِذَلِكَ وِلَايَتَهُ وَيُزِيلُونَ وَلَاءَهُ فَقَالَ ذَلِكَ فِيهِ لِيَنْفِيَ ذَلِكَ عَنْهُ فِي وَقْتِهِ وَبَعْدِهِ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى لَوْ عَلِمَ أَنَّ عَلِيّاً سَيُفَارِقُ الدِّينَ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ أَوْ غَيْرِهِ عَلَى مَا قُرِفَ بِهِ لَمْ يَأْمُرْ نَبِيَّهُ أَنْ يَأْمُرَ النَّاسَ بِاعْتِقَادِ وِلَايَاتِهِ وَمَحَبَّتِهِ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَالْقَطْعِ عَلَى طَهَارَتِهِ وَهُوَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ يَخْتِمُ عَمَلَهُ بِمُفَارَقَةِ الدِّينِ لِأَنَّ مَنْ هَذِهِ سَبِيلُهُ فِي مَعْلُومِ اللهِ تَعَالَى فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَطُّ وَلِيّاً لِلَّهِ وَلَا مِمَّنْ يَسْتَحِقُّ الْوِلَايَةَ وَالْمَحَبَّةَ، وَفِي أَمْرِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِمُوَالَاةِ عَلِيٍّ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى سُقُوطِ مَا قَرَفَهُ أَهْلُ النِّفَاقِ وَالضَّلَالِ بِهِ .
فَإِنْ قَالُوا : فَإِذَا كَانَ هَذَا هُوَ الَّذِي أَرَادَهُ فَلِمَ لَمْ يَقُلْ : عَلِيٌّ مُؤْمِنُ الظَّاهِرِ وَالْبَاطِنِ نَقِيُّ السَّرِيرَةِ وَخَاتِمُ لِعَمَلِهِ بِالْبِرِّ وَالطَّاعَةِ فَيُزِيلُ الْإِشْكَالَ؟ قِيلَ لَهُمْ : لَيْسَ لَنَا الِاعْتِرَاضُ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي تَخَيُّرِ الْأَلْفَاظِ وَلَعَلَّهُ أُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِ أَنَّ إِذَاعَةَ هَذَا الْكَلَامِ وَجَمْعَ النَّاسِ لَهُ وَتَقْدِيمَ التَّقْرِيرِ لِوُجُوبِ طَاعَتِهِ لُطْفٌ لِعَلِيٍّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَأَنَّهُ أَجْمَعُ لِلْقُلُوبِ عَلَى مَحَبَّتِهِ وَمُوَالَاتِهِ فَلَا سُؤَالَ عَلَيْنَا فِي ذَلِكَ .
ثُمَّ يُقَالُ لَهُمْ : فَلَوْ كَانَ الرَّسُولُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِنَّمَا أَرَادَ بِهَذَا الْقَوْلِ النَّصَّ عَلَيْهِ فَلِمَ لَمْ يَقُلْ : هَذَا إِمَامُكُمْ بَعْدِي الْوَاجِبَةُ طَاعَتُهُ فَاسْمَعُوا لَهُ وَأَطِيعُوا فَيُزِيلُ الْوَهْمَ وَالْإِشْكَالَ ؟ فَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ أَجَابُوا بِهِ، فَهُوَ جَوَابٌ لَهُمْ فِيمَا سَأَلُوا عَنْهُ .
Clients of alliance, not clients of kinship, but dependents who press pine nuts. As for what the Prophet (peace be upon him) intended by his statement: 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla,' it can bear two meanings: one of them is: whoever I am his supporter in his religion and his defender, in my apparent and hidden, secret and public, then Ali is his supporter in this way; so the benefit of that is the informing that Ali's hidden and apparent are equal in supporting the religion and the believers, and certainty about his inner state and high rank. And that is not believed about every apparent supporter of the believers, because the supporter may support with his apparent seeking hypocrisy and reputation and seeking reward and worldly goods. So when the Prophet (peace be upon him) informed that the support of some of the believers in the religion and the Muslims is like his own support (peace be upon him), certainty is made about the purity of his inner state and soundness of his hidden, and this is a great virtue. And it is also possible that the intended meaning of his statement: 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla' is: whoever I am beloved to him and a friend to him in my apparent and hidden, then Ali is his mawla, meaning that his friendship and love in his apparent and hidden are obligatory just as my friendship and love in this way are obligatory. So he has made obligatory his friendship in his apparent and hidden, and we do not befriend everyone who manifests faith in this way, but rather we befriend them in apparent only, not in hidden. If it is said: What is the reason for singling him out with this statement when among you there were many Companions whose apparent was like their hidden? It is said to him: It is possible that it reached him (peace be upon him) a disparagement of a disparager or a slander of a slanderer, or he was informed that a group from the people of hypocrisy and the Kharijites would attack him and claim that he had left the religion and judged in God's matter concerning humans, and thereby they would nullify his friendship and remove his loyalty. So he said that concerning him to negate that from him in his time and after, because if God knew that Ali would leave the religion by arbitration or otherwise according to what he was accused of, He would not have commanded His Prophet to command people to believe in his friendship and love in his apparent and hidden and to be certain of his purity, while He knew that he would end his life by leaving the religion. For whoever is such in God's knowledge, he was never a friend of God nor among those who deserve friendship and love. And in the command of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) to befriend Ali in his apparent and hidden is evidence of the fall of what the people of hypocrisy and misguidance accused him of. Then they said: If this is what he intended, why did he not say: 'Ali is a believer in apparent and hidden, pure of inner state, and his work ends with piety and obedience' to remove ambiguity? It was said to them: We have no objection to the Prophet (peace be upon him) in choosing words; perhaps it was revealed to him that publicizing this speech, gathering people for it, and presenting the affirmation of the obligation of obedience to him was a kindness for Ali (peace be upon him) and that it is more gathering of hearts for his love and friendship. So there is no question upon us in that. Then it is said to them: If the Messenger (peace be upon him) intended by this statement explicit appointment of him, why did he not say: 'This is your imam after me, obedience to whom is obligatory, so listen to him and obey' to remove doubt and ambiguity? Whatever they answer with, it is an answer for them regarding what they asked about.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a response to a Shiite claim that the Prophet's statement 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla' constitutes explicit appointment (nass) of Ali as successor. The author, Imam al-Baqillani, begins by quoting a line of poetry that distinguishes between two types of mawla: by alliance (hulf) and by kinship. This sets the stage that the word 'mawla' can have multiple meanings. He then states that the Prophet's statement can bear two meanings. First, 'mawla' means supporter or helper (nasir). In this interpretation, the Prophet is informing that Ali's hidden and apparent support for the religion is equal to his own, a great virtue, but not every apparent supporter is like that because some support for show. Second, 'mawla' means beloved and friend (mahbub wali). In this interpretation, the Prophet is obligating love and friendship for Ali both outwardly and inwardly, just as the Prophet himself is to be loved. This does not mean political succession. Then an objection is raised: Why single out Ali when many Companions were sincerely faithful? The answer is that the Prophet foresaw that hypocrites and Kharijites would slander Ali, claiming he left the religion, so this statement was to refute that slander in advance. God would not command belief in Ali's friendship if He knew Ali would apostatize. Thus the statement proves the falsehood of the accusations. A further objection: Why didn't the Prophet say explicitly 'Ali is a believer inside and out' to avoid confusion? The answer: We do not object to the Prophet's choice of words; God perhaps inspired this phrasing to gather people's hearts to love Ali. Another objection: If the Prophet intended appointment, why not say 'This is your imam after me'? The author then turns the argument, saying that any response the opponents give to that question can also be applied to their own objection. This is a classic kalam rhetorical move to show inconsistency in the opponent's position.

Key Terms
مولاه (mawla)
نفاق (hypocrisy)
شُراة (Kharijites)
ولاية (wila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's singling out of Ali implies he is the only one worthy of such praise, and therefore the intended successor.
Correction: Baqillani explains the singling out was due to specific slander that would target Ali, not because he was superior to all others in every way.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why did the Prophet single out Ali in his statement?
A) Because Ali was the most virtuous Companion
B) Because the Prophet wanted to emphasize succession
C) Because the Prophet foresaw future slander against Ali
D) Because the Companions asked him to

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's statement was a defense against future slander, proving Ali's sincerity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet (peace be upon him) were to make a statement about your apparent and hidden character, would you be confident that your interior matches your exterior? What specific hidden attitudes do you need to align with what you show others?
?
The lesson argues that God would not command people to love someone He knows will end up a hypocrite. Now think about someone you claim to love for Allah's sake: are you fully certain of their sincerity? And more importantly, how does this truth challenge you to examine the sincerity of your own loyalties, knowing that God knows your future?
?
Imagine that you are the target of slander and false accusations, just as Ali was. The Prophet's defense of him was based on divine knowledge and future slander. What would it mean for you to trust that Allah has already prepared a defense for you, even if no one defends you now? How does this lesson change the way you react to slander against you?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
7 min
Further Objections and the Final Counter-Argument
Baqillani addresses further objections and presents a counter-argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani responds to two further objections—why the Prophet did not simply say 'Ali is a believer' and why he did not explicitly say 'this is your imam'—and then turns the argument back on the opponents, showing the inconsistency of their position.

Core Idea
Baqillani uses the opponents' own logic against them.

Baqillani continues with two more objections: Why didn't the Prophet just say 'Ali is a believer inside and out' to avoid confusion? And if he intended appointment, why not say 'This is your imam after me'? Baqillani's responses and his final counter-argument cleverly expose the weakness in the opposing view. This lesson completes his defense.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first objection
The opponents argue: If the Prophet meant to affirm Ali's sincerity, why didn't he just say 'Ali is a believer inside and out'? This would have removed ambiguity.
This objection assumes the Prophet's wording was unnecessarily indirect.
2
See Baqillani's response
Baqillani says we do not object to the Prophet's choice of words; perhaps God inspired this phrasing to gather people's hearts. It is not for us to question divine wisdom.
This is a deferential response that rejects the premise that the wording was inadequate.
3
Examine the second objection and the counter-argument
The opponents then say: If the Prophet intended appointment, why didn't he say 'This is your imam after me'? Baqillani turns this around: Whatever answer they give to that question (e.g., the wording was sufficient), it applies equally to their own objection about the original hadith. Thus their argument is self-defeating.
This is a classic logical retort.

مَوَالِيَ حِلْفٍ لَا مَوَالِيَ قَرَابَةٍ وَلَكِنْ قَطِيناً يَعْصِرُونَ الصَّنَوْبَرَا فَأَمَّا مَا قَصَدَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِقَوْلِهِ: «مَنْ كُنْتُ مَوْلَاهُ، فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ» فَإِنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ أَمْرَيْنِ أَحَدُهُمَا مَنْ كُنْتُ نَاصِرَهُ عَلَى دِينِهِ وَحَامِياً عَنْهُ بِظَاهِرِي وَبَاطِنِي وَسِرِّي وَعَلَانِيَتِي فَعَلِيٌّ نَاصِرُهُ عَلَى هَذَا السَّبِيلِ فَتَكُونُ فَائِدَةُ ذَلِكَ الْإِخْبَارُ عَنْ أَنَّ بَاطِنَ عَلِيٍّ وَظَاهِرَهُ فِي نُصْرَةِ الدِّينِ وَالْمُؤْمِنِينَ سَوَاءٌ وَالْقَطْعَ عَلَى سَرِيرَتِهِ وَعُلُوِّ رُتْبَتِهِ ; وَلَيْسَ يُعْتَقَدُ ذَلِكَ فِي كُلِّ نَاصِرٍ لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ بِظَاهِرِهِ ; لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَنْصُرُ النَّاصِرُ بِظَاهِرِهِ طَلَبَ النِّفَاقِ وَالسُّمْعَةِ وَابْتِغَاءَ الرِّفْدِ وَمَتَاعِ الدُّنْيَا فَإِذَا أَخْبَرَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَّ نُصْرَةَ بَعْضِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي الدِّينِ وَالْمُسْلِمِينَ كَنُصْرَتِهِ هُوَ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قُطِعَ عَلَى طَهَارَةِ سَرِيرَتِهِ وَسَلَامَةِ بَاطِنِهِ وَهَذِهِ فَضِيلَةٌ عَظِيمَةٌ. وَيَحْتَمِلُ أَيْضاً أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُرَادُ بِقَوْلِهِ : «فَمَنْ كُنْتُ مَوْلَاهُ فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ»، أَيْ مَنْ كُنْتُ مَحْبُوباً عِنْدَهُ وَوَلِيّاً لَهُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِي وَبَاطِنِي فَعَلِيٌّ مَوْلَاهُ أَيْ إِنَّ وِلَاءَهُ وَمَحَبَّتَهُ مِنْ ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَاجِبٌ كَمَا أَنَّ وِلَائِي وَمَحَبَّتِي عَلَى هَذَا السَّبِيلِ وَاجِبٌ فَيَكُونُ قَدْ أَوْجَبَ مُوَالَاتَهُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَلَسْنَا نُوَالِي كُلَّ مَنْ ظَهَرَ مِنْهُ الْإِيمَانُ عَلَى هَذِهِ السَّبِيلِ بَلْ إِنَّمَا نُوَالِيهِمْ فِي الظَّاهِرِ دُونَ الْبَاطِنِ .
فَإِنْ قِيلَ : فَمَا وَجْهُ تَخْصِيصِهِ بِهَذَا الْقَوْلِ وَقَدْ كَانَ عِنْدَكُمْ فِي الصَّحَابَةِ خَلْقٌ عَظِيمٌ ظَاهِرُهُمْ كَبَاطِنِهِمْ؟ قِيلَ لَهُ : يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ بَلَغَهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَدْحُ قَادِحٍ فِيهِ أَوْ ثَلْبُ ثَالِبٍ أَوْ أَخْبَرَ أَنَّ قَوْماً مِنْ أَهْلِ النِّفَاقِ وَالشُّرَاةِ سَيَطْعَنُونَ عَلَيْهِ وَيَزْعُمُونَ أَنَّهُ فَارَقَ الدِّينَ وَحَكَمَ فِي أَمْرِ اللهِ تَعَالَى الْآدَمِيِّينَ وَيُسْقِطُونَ بِذَلِكَ وِلَايَتَهُ وَيُزِيلُونَ وَلَاءَهُ فَقَالَ ذَلِكَ فِيهِ لِيَنْفِيَ ذَلِكَ عَنْهُ فِي وَقْتِهِ وَبَعْدِهِ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى لَوْ عَلِمَ أَنَّ عَلِيّاً سَيُفَارِقُ الدِّينَ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ أَوْ غَيْرِهِ عَلَى مَا قُرِفَ بِهِ لَمْ يَأْمُرْ نَبِيَّهُ أَنْ يَأْمُرَ النَّاسَ بِاعْتِقَادِ وِلَايَاتِهِ وَمَحَبَّتِهِ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ وَالْقَطْعِ عَلَى طَهَارَتِهِ وَهُوَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ يَخْتِمُ عَمَلَهُ بِمُفَارَقَةِ الدِّينِ لِأَنَّ مَنْ هَذِهِ سَبِيلُهُ فِي مَعْلُومِ اللهِ تَعَالَى فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَطُّ وَلِيّاً لِلَّهِ وَلَا مِمَّنْ يَسْتَحِقُّ الْوِلَايَةَ وَالْمَحَبَّةَ، وَفِي أَمْرِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِمُوَالَاةِ عَلِيٍّ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَبَاطِنِهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى سُقُوطِ مَا قَرَفَهُ أَهْلُ النِّفَاقِ وَالضَّلَالِ بِهِ .
فَإِنْ قَالُوا : فَإِذَا كَانَ هَذَا هُوَ الَّذِي أَرَادَهُ فَلِمَ لَمْ يَقُلْ : عَلِيٌّ مُؤْمِنُ الظَّاهِرِ وَالْبَاطِنِ نَقِيُّ السَّرِيرَةِ وَخَاتِمُ لِعَمَلِهِ بِالْبِرِّ وَالطَّاعَةِ فَيُزِيلُ الْإِشْكَالَ؟ قِيلَ لَهُمْ : لَيْسَ لَنَا الِاعْتِرَاضُ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي تَخَيُّرِ الْأَلْفَاظِ وَلَعَلَّهُ أُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِ أَنَّ إِذَاعَةَ هَذَا الْكَلَامِ وَجَمْعَ النَّاسِ لَهُ وَتَقْدِيمَ التَّقْرِيرِ لِوُجُوبِ طَاعَتِهِ لُطْفٌ لِعَلِيٍّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَأَنَّهُ أَجْمَعُ لِلْقُلُوبِ عَلَى مَحَبَّتِهِ وَمُوَالَاتِهِ فَلَا سُؤَالَ عَلَيْنَا فِي ذَلِكَ .
ثُمَّ يُقَالُ لَهُمْ : فَلَوْ كَانَ الرَّسُولُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِنَّمَا أَرَادَ بِهَذَا الْقَوْلِ النَّصَّ عَلَيْهِ فَلِمَ لَمْ يَقُلْ : هَذَا إِمَامُكُمْ بَعْدِي الْوَاجِبَةُ طَاعَتُهُ فَاسْمَعُوا لَهُ وَأَطِيعُوا فَيُزِيلُ الْوَهْمَ وَالْإِشْكَالَ ؟ فَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ أَجَابُوا بِهِ، فَهُوَ جَوَابٌ لَهُمْ فِيمَا سَأَلُوا عَنْهُ .
Clients of alliance, not clients of kinship, but dependents who press pine nuts. As for what the Prophet (peace be upon him) intended by his statement: 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla,' it can bear two meanings: one of them is: whoever I am his supporter in his religion and his defender, in my apparent and hidden, secret and public, then Ali is his supporter in this way; so the benefit of that is the informing that Ali's hidden and apparent are equal in supporting the religion and the believers, and certainty about his inner state and high rank. And that is not believed about every apparent supporter of the believers, because the supporter may support with his apparent seeking hypocrisy and reputation and seeking reward and worldly goods. So when the Prophet (peace be upon him) informed that the support of some of the believers in the religion and the Muslims is like his own support (peace be upon him), certainty is made about the purity of his inner state and soundness of his hidden, and this is a great virtue. And it is also possible that the intended meaning of his statement: 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla' is: whoever I am beloved to him and a friend to him in my apparent and hidden, then Ali is his mawla, meaning that his friendship and love in his apparent and hidden are obligatory just as my friendship and love in this way are obligatory. So he has made obligatory his friendship in his apparent and hidden, and we do not befriend everyone who manifests faith in this way, but rather we befriend them in apparent only, not in hidden. If it is said: What is the reason for singling him out with this statement when among you there were many Companions whose apparent was like their hidden? It is said to him: It is possible that it reached him (peace be upon him) a disparagement of a disparager or a slander of a slanderer, or he was informed that a group from the people of hypocrisy and the Kharijites would attack him and claim that he had left the religion and judged in God's matter concerning humans, and thereby they would nullify his friendship and remove his loyalty. So he said that concerning him to negate that from him in his time and after, because if God knew that Ali would leave the religion by arbitration or otherwise according to what he was accused of, He would not have commanded His Prophet to command people to believe in his friendship and love in his apparent and hidden and to be certain of his purity, while He knew that he would end his life by leaving the religion. For whoever is such in God's knowledge, he was never a friend of God nor among those who deserve friendship and love. And in the command of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) to befriend Ali in his apparent and hidden is evidence of the fall of what the people of hypocrisy and misguidance accused him of. Then they said: If this is what he intended, why did he not say: 'Ali is a believer in apparent and hidden, pure of inner state, and his work ends with piety and obedience' to remove ambiguity? It was said to them: We have no objection to the Prophet (peace be upon him) in choosing words; perhaps it was revealed to him that publicizing this speech, gathering people for it, and presenting the affirmation of the obligation of obedience to him was a kindness for Ali (peace be upon him) and that it is more gathering of hearts for his love and friendship. So there is no question upon us in that. Then it is said to them: If the Messenger (peace be upon him) intended by this statement explicit appointment of him, why did he not say: 'This is your imam after me, obedience to whom is obligatory, so listen to him and obey' to remove doubt and ambiguity? Whatever they answer with, it is an answer for them regarding what they asked about.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a response to a Shiite claim that the Prophet's statement 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla' constitutes explicit appointment (nass) of Ali as successor. The author, Imam al-Baqillani, begins by quoting a line of poetry that distinguishes between two types of mawla: by alliance (hulf) and by kinship. This sets the stage that the word 'mawla' can have multiple meanings. He then states that the Prophet's statement can bear two meanings. First, 'mawla' means supporter or helper (nasir). In this interpretation, the Prophet is informing that Ali's hidden and apparent support for the religion is equal to his own, a great virtue, but not every apparent supporter is like that because some support for show. Second, 'mawla' means beloved and friend (mahbub wali). In this interpretation, the Prophet is obligating love and friendship for Ali both outwardly and inwardly, just as the Prophet himself is to be loved. This does not mean political succession. Then an objection is raised: Why single out Ali when many Companions were sincerely faithful? The answer is that the Prophet foresaw that hypocrites and Kharijites would slander Ali, claiming he left the religion, so this statement was to refute that slander in advance. God would not command belief in Ali's friendship if He knew Ali would apostatize. Thus the statement proves the falsehood of the accusations. A further objection: Why didn't the Prophet say explicitly 'Ali is a believer inside and out' to avoid confusion? The answer: We do not object to the Prophet's choice of words; God perhaps inspired this phrasing to gather people's hearts to love Ali. Another objection: If the Prophet intended appointment, why not say 'This is your imam after me'? The author then turns the argument, saying that any response the opponents give to that question can also be applied to their own objection. This is a classic kalam rhetorical move to show inconsistency in the opponent's position.

Key Terms
مولاه (mawla)
نص (explicit appointment)
إمام (imam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's wording was insufficient or ambiguous, so the hadith cannot be used as proof of anything.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the Prophet's words are perfect; we do not object to them. The ambiguity is not a flaw but a deliberate choice with wise purpose.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's counter-argument to the objection that the Prophet should have said 'This is your imam after me'?
A) The Prophet was not allowed to say that
B) Whatever answer they give applies to their own objection
C) The hadith is not about imamah
D) Ali forbade the Prophet from saying that

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that any objection raised about clarity applies equally to the opponents' own view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Prophet's words, do you trust that every word was divinely guided, or do you find yourself criticizing why he didn't say something differently? What does that reveal about your heart's submission to his authority?
?
Think of a time when you demanded explicit, undeniable proof from Allah before obeying a difficult command. How does Baqillani's trust in the Prophet's wisdom challenge you to accept implicit guidance with faith?
?
The opponents' logic was inconsistent: they expected one standard for clarity but applied another. Where in your own life do you hold others to a different standard than yourself? How can you align your expectations with the prophetic example?

Refutation of the 'You are to Me as Harun to Musa' Hadith Claim
Baqillani refutes the claim that the hadith 'You are to me as Harun to Musa' implies Ali's succession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the hadith 'You are to me as Harun to Musa' does not imply Ali's succession according to al-Baqillani, and how historical context refutes the claim.

Core Idea
The hadith refers to temporary deputyship during Tabuk, not general succession.

This lesson presents al-Baqillani's response to another Shiite proof-text based on a well-known hadith. By examining the historical context of the Prophet's statement, he shows that the comparison to Harun is limited to a specific occasion, not a universal designation of succession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the structure: the opponents' claim and Baqillani's response.
2
Identify the claim
The opponents argue that the Prophet's statement 'You are to me as Harun to Musa' is an explicit appointment (nass) of Ali as successor, by analogy to Harun's role.
Note the exception 'except there is no prophet after me'.
3
Examine the refutation
Baqillani responds that the interpretation is not necessary because the statement was made in a specific context: the Prophet was appointing Ali as deputy over his family and Medina during the Tabuk expedition, not as general successor.
4
Consider the historical context
The hypocrites spread rumors that the Prophet left Ali behind out of hatred. To counter this, the Prophet said the hadith. So the comparison to Harun is about temporary deputyship, not succession.
The narrator Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas reported that Ali caught up with the Prophet to ask about this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دَلِيلٌ آخَرُ
فَإِنْ قَالُوا مَا أَنْكَرْتُمْ أَنْ يَكُونَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَصَّ عَلَى عَلِيٍّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بِقَوْلِهِ : أَنْتَ مِنِّي بِمَنْزِلَةِ هَارُونَ مِنْ مُوسَى ; إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا نَبِيَّ بَعْدِي »؟ قِيلَ لَهُمْ : لَا يَجِبُ ذَلِكَ ; لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى ذَلِكَ أَنِّي أَسْتَخْلِفُكَ عَلَى أَهْلِي وَعَلَى الْمَدِينَةِ إِذَا تَوَجَّهْتُ إِلَى هَذِهِ الْغَزْوَةِ لِأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا قَالَ ذَلِكَ فِي غَزَاةِ تَبُوكَ لَمَّا خَلَّفَهُ بِالْمَدِينَةِ وَمَاجَ أَهْلُ النِّفَاقِ وَأَكْثَرُوا وَقَالُوا : قَدْ أَبْغَضَ عَلِيّاً وَقَلَاهُ ; وَقَالَ سَعْدُ بْنُ أَبِي وَقَّاصٍ (۲) ، وَهُوَ الْعُمْدَةُ فِي رِوَايَةِ هَذَا الْحَدِيثِ : فَلَحِقَ عَلِيٌّ ...
Another proof. If they say: What prevents you from [accepting] that the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly appointed Ali (peace be upon him) by his statement: 'You are to me in the position of Harun to Musa, except that there is no prophet after me'? It is said to them: That is not necessary, because the meaning of that is: I appoint you as my deputy over my family and over the city when I set out for this expedition, for he only said that during the expedition of Tabuk when he left him behind in Medina, and the people of hypocrisy stirred and spoke much and said: 'He has hated Ali and abandoned him'; and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, who is the main narrator of this hadith, said: So Ali caught up...
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of another Shiite proof-text: the hadith 'You are to me as Harun to Musa, except that there is no prophet after me.' The author, al-Baqillani, presents this as a separate argument (dafil akhar) from the opponents. He states that the opponents claim that this hadith constitutes explicit appointment (nass) of Ali as successor, by analogy to Harun being Musa's successor and brother. The response is that this interpretation is not necessary (la yajibu dhalik). The true meaning is that the Prophet was appointing Ali as his deputy over his family and Medina for the specific occasion of the Tabuk expedition. The historical context is given: the Prophet left Ali behind in Medina when he went to Tabuk. The hypocrites spread rumors that the Prophet hated Ali and left him behind because of that. To refute these rumors, the Prophet said this hadith. Thus, the comparison to Harun is limited to temporary deputyship (istikhilaf) during a campaign, not general succession. The author also mentions that Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, the main narrator of the hadith, reported that Ali caught up with the Prophet to ask about this, and the Prophet reassured him. The passage ends abruptly at 'so Ali caught up', but the argument is complete: the hadith is about a specific context, not a general designation of succession.

Key Terms
نص (nass)
بمنزلة هارون (in the position of Harun)
استخلاف (deputyship)
غزوة تبوك (Tabuk expedition)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith 'You are to me as Harun to Musa' implies that Ali is the Prophet's successor in all matters, including leadership of the community.
Correction: The hadith was said in a specific context (Tabuk) about temporary deputyship over family and city, not general succession. The exception 'except there is no prophet after me' excludes prophethood, but the deputyship is limited to that occasion.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani, what was the historical context of the Prophet's statement 'You are to me as Harun to Musa'?
A) During the conquest of Mecca
B) During the expedition of Tabuk when Ali was left behind in Medina
C) At the deathbed of the Prophet
D) At the Battle of Badr

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'You are to me as Harun to Musa' refers to a specific incident during the Tabuk expedition and does not constitute a general designation of succession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a time you used a verse or hadith to support your own opinion without checking its context. What would you have to do to uncover the true meaning, and are you willing to do that even if it challenges your view?
?
The hypocrites twisted the Prophet's action of leaving Ali behind into a sign of hatred. Can you point to a moment this week where you misinterpreted someone's action or words? What would it take to suspend judgment until you know the full story?
?
The Prophet's refutation of the claim about Ali is based on historical facts. How often do you verify the facts behind claims you hear about Islam or Muslims? Will you commit to verifying one contentious claim this week?

Refuting the Claim that the Hadith of Position Implies Succession
Author refutes claim that 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses' implies succession after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Hadith of Position (حديث المنزلة) does not prove that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as his successor after his death, and how the context of the Tabuk expedition and the stations of Aaron limit its meaning.

Core Idea
The Hadith of Position refers only to temporary vicegerency during the Tabuk campaign, not to succession after death.

This lesson tackles a key argument used to claim that the Prophet explicitly appointed Ali as his successor. The argument relies on the well-known hadith, 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses, except that there is no prophet after me.' Imam al-Baqillani dismantles this argument by examining the historical context of the hadith and the actual relationship between Aaron and Moses. He shows that the Prophet's words were a comfort to Ali during a specific military campaign, not a general declaration of succession after death.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the immediate response
Start by reading the first part of the passage where the objection is presented. Notice how the author immediately denies that the hadith necessarily implies succession. Then read his initial response about the context of the Tabuk expedition.
The key is to see that the author does not reject the hadith; he reinterprets it within its proper context.
2
Understand the story of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas
The author includes a report from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas to explain why the Prophet said those words. Ali was upset at being left behind, and the Prophet reassured him. This shows the purpose was to dispel rumors, not to designate a successor.
This narrative is essential for understanding the emotional and situational context.
3
Analyze the stations of Aaron
The author lists three stations Aaron had with Moses: brotherhood, partnership in prophethood, and vicegerency during absence. He then points out that succession after death was not among them, because Aaron died before Moses. Therefore, the analogy cannot include that meaning.
This logical reasoning is the core of the refutation.
4
Draw the conclusion
The author concludes that the Prophet's intended meaning was limited to vicegerency during the Tabuk expedition, as Moses left Aaron in charge when he went to speak with his Lord. This is the only meaning consistent with the historical facts.
Notice how the author uses 'it is not permissible' to emphasize the certainty of his interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا ما أنكرتم أن يكون النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نص على علي عليه السلام بقوله: أنت مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى إلا أنه لا نبي بعدي؟ قيل لهم: لا يجب ذلك؛ لأن معنى ذلك أني أستخلفك على أهلي وعلى المدينة إذا توجهت إلى هذه الغزوة لأنه إنما قال ذلك في غزاة تبوك لما خلفه بالمدينة وماج أهل النفاق وأكثروا وقالوا: قد أبغض علياً وقلاه. وقال سعد بن أبي وقاص وهو العمدة في رواية هذا الحديث: فلحق علي بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: يا رسول الله، أتتركني مع الأخلاف؟ فقال: أما ترضى أن تكون مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى بعدي؟ أي إني لم أخلفك بغضاً ولا قلى كما أن موسى لم يخلف أخاه هارون في بني إسرائيل لما توجه لكلام ربه بغضاً ولا قلى. ومما يدل على أن هذا المعنى هو الذي قصده بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم علمنا أنه كان لهارون من موسى منازل منها أنه كان أخاه، ومنها أنه كان شريكاً له في النبوة، ومنها أنه خلفه في قومه لما توجه لكلام ربه؛ وليس منها أنه خلفه بعد موته لأن هارون مات قبل موسى بسنين كثيرة وإنما خلف موسى بعد موته يوشع بن نون؛ فلا يجوز أن يكون النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إنما عنى بقوله: أنت مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى أي إنك أخي لأبي وأمي ولا أنك تخلفني بعد موتي لأن هذه منزلة لم تكن لهارون من موسى؛ فثبت أنه إنما أراد أنك خليفتي على أهلي وعلى المدينة عند توجهي إلى هذه الغزوة كما خلف موسى أخوه هارون في قومه عند توجهه لكلام ربه.
For if they say: What prevents you from acknowledging that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) explicitly designated Ali (عليه السلام) by his saying: 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses, except that there is no prophet after me'? It is said to them: That is not necessarily so; because the meaning of that is: I appoint you as my vicegerent over my family and over the city when I set out for this expedition, since he only said that in the campaign of Tabuk when he left him behind in Medina, and the people of hypocrisy stirred and spoke much, saying: He has hated Ali and forsaken him. And Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas — who is the primary authority in narrating this hadith — said: So Ali caught up with the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) and said: O Messenger of Allah, do you leave me with the women and children? He said: Are you not pleased that you are to me as Aaron was to Moses, except that there is no prophet after me? Meaning: I have not left you behind out of hatred or aversion, just as Moses did not leave behind his brother Aaron among the Children of Israel when he went to speak with his Lord out of hatred or aversion. And among what indicates that this meaning is what he intended by his saying (صلى الله عليه وسلم) is our knowledge that Aaron had stations with Moses: from them is that he was his brother, from them is that he was his partner in prophethood, and from them is that he was his vicegerent over his people when he went to speak with his Lord; and it is not among them that he succeeded him after his death, because Aaron died many years before Moses, and indeed Moses was succeeded after his death by Joshua son of Nun. So it is not permissible that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) meant by his saying 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses': that you are my brother from my father and mother, nor that you will succeed me after my death, because this station was not for Aaron from Moses. Thus it is established that he only meant: You are my vicegerent over my family and over the city at my setting out for this expedition, just as Moses' brother Aaron was vicegerent over his people when he went to speak with his Lord.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific argument used by those who claim that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as his successor. The argument is based on the famous hadith: 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses, except that there is no prophet after me.' The author first presents the objection: how can the author deny that this is an explicit designation? The author's answer begins by denying that this necessarily follows. He explains that the context of the hadith is the campaign of Tabuk, when the Prophet left Ali behind in Medina. At that time, hypocrites spread rumours that the Prophet had left Ali because he hated him. Ali followed the Prophet and asked if he was being left with the women and children. The Prophet comforted him with the analogy to Aaron, meaning: just as Moses left Aaron in charge of his people during his absence—not out of hatred—so I leave you in charge here. The author then provides additional evidence: we know that Aaron had several stations with Moses: brotherhood, partnership in prophethood, and vicegerency during Moses' absence. Crucially, succession after death was not one of these stations, because Aaron died before Moses. The actual successor after Moses' death was Joshua. Therefore, the Prophet could not have meant absolute succession after his own death. Instead, the intended meaning is limited to vicegerency during the specific absence for the Tabuk expedition. The passage follows a clear logical order: objection, initial contextual rebuttal, and a second argument based on the known stations of Aaron.

Key Terms
نص
منزلة
خليفة
هارون
غزوة تبوك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses' proves that Ali was the Prophet's immediate successor after his death.
Correction: The hadith was said in the context of the Tabuk expedition and refers only to temporary vicegerency during the Prophet's absence. Aaron himself did not succeed Moses after death, as he died before him.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Baqillani, what is the correct interpretation of the Prophet's statement 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses'?
A) It establishes Ali as the Prophet's brother and successor after his death.
B) It means Ali is the vicegerent over the family and Medina during the Tabuk expedition, not after death.
C) It indicates that Ali shares in prophethood with the Prophet.
D) It is a general statement of love and has no specific meaning.

Key Takeaway
The Hadith of Position does not imply succession after death; it was a contextual reassurance about temporary vicegerency during the Tabuk campaign.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a religious claim based on a single hadith without investigating its full context? How does this lesson challenge you to verify your understanding before holding firm beliefs? Be honest: what is one belief you hold that might benefit from such scrutiny?
?
This passage shows the Prophet reassuring Ali with the Aaron analogy to dispel doubts about his love. When you feel abandoned or undervalued by those you respect, do you seek their reassurance or assume the worst? How can this prophetic example reshape your response to perceived rejection?
?
The author argues that interpreting the hadith as succession would contradict known facts about Aaron's life. When your own opinions conflict with clear evidence, do you adjust your views or cling to them? What will it cost you to let go of a cherished interpretation that does not hold up to examination? Become specific: name one time you chose comfort over truth.

Why 'Brother and Vicegerent' Does Not Prove Imamate
Baqillani refutes the argument that the Prophet's statement to Ali is a nass on imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the Prophet's statement to Ali does not constitute a clear text (nass) for imamate.

Core Idea
Praise and delegation of a specific task do not imply universal succession.

In this passage, Baqillani responds to a key Shi'a proof-text for Ali's imamate: the Prophet's statement 'You are my brother and my vicegerent over my family...' Baqillani shows that this statement, even if authentic, does not designate Ali as the imam after the Prophet. He breaks down the meaning of each phrase and draws an analogy to illustrate the point.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Notice the Shi'a claim uses several phrases: brother, vicegerent over my family, payer of debts, fulfiller of promises. Consider why they think these imply imamate.
2
Follow Baqillani's response
He argues that 'brother' is honorific, 'vicegerent' is limited to family, 'payer of debts' is a specific task, and none imply imamate. Identify each point.
3
Consider the analogy
Baqillani says if a current caliph said similar words about someone, it wouldn't be a nass. Reflect on how this analogy strengthens his argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل آخر
فإن قالوا ما أنكرتم أن يكون النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم قد نص على عليّ بقوله : «أنت أخي وخليفتي في أهلي وقاضي ديني ومنجز عداتي» ؟ قيل لهم : ليس في هذا أيضاً لو ثبت نص على إمامته لأنه إذا أراد بقوله «أخي» التعظيم لم يكن هذا عهداً في الإمامة ولا من النص على ولايته في شيء؛ وإن كان ذلك خبراً له عن فضله وعظيم محله منه وأمانته في نفسه وهو أيضاً خليفته على أهله فاطمة وولدها عليهم السلام، وقوله : وقاضي ديني متوجه إلى أنه أمره بقضاء دينه أو كان قد قضي عنه قبل هذا القول؛ وليس هذا من قوله أنت الإمام بعدي في شيء؛ ولهذا لو قال خليفة الأمة في هذا الوقت زيد هذا أخي وخليفتي في أهلي وقاضي ديني لم يكن هذا عهداً إليه في الإمامة ولا من النص على ولايته في شيء، وإن كان ذلك خبراً عن فضله عنده وعظيم محله منه وأمانته وثقته؛ فلا متعلق أيضاً في هذا القول .
Another proof: If they say: 'What prevents you from acknowledging that the Prophet ﷺ explicitly designated Ali by his saying: "You are my brother, my vicegerent over my family, the one who pays my debts, and the fulfiller of my promises"?' It is said to them: Even if this is established, it does not constitute a text for his imamate, because if he meant by his saying 'brother' exaltation, this is not a covenant for imamate nor anything from the nass on his authority. And if that is news of his virtue and his great status with him and his trustworthiness in himself, and also his vicegerent over his family Fatima and her children (peace be upon them). And his saying 'and the one who pays my debts' is directed to that he ordered him to pay his debt or that it had been paid before this statement. And this is not from his saying 'you are the imam after me' in any way. For this reason, if the caliph of the community at this time were to say 'Zaid is my brother and my vicegerent over my family and the one who pays my debts,' this would not be a covenant to him for imamate nor from the nass on his authority in anything, even if it were news of his virtue with him and his great status and trustworthiness. So there is no support in this statement either.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a argument that the Prophet's statement to Ali constitutes a clear text (nass) on his imamate. The author first presents the objection: the opponents claim the Prophet said, 'You are my brother, my vicegerent over my family, the one who pays my debts, and the fulfiller of my promises.' Then the answer is given in several points: 1) If the word 'brother' is meant as an honorific, it does not imply a covenant of imamate. 2) Even if it is a report of Ali's virtue and trustworthiness, it only makes him the Prophet's deputy over his household (Fatima and her children), not over the entire umma. 3) The phrase 'the one who pays my debts' refers to a specific task of settling debts, not to succession. 4) By analogy, if a current caliph said such words about someone, it would not be considered a designation for imamate. Therefore, this statement provides no support for their claim.

Key Terms
النص
الإمامة
الخلافة
العهد
الولاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any statement of praise or delegation of a specific task from the Prophet constitutes a clear text (nass) for imamate.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the words in question are either honorific, limited in scope, or specific to a task, and do not imply universal succession. An analogy with a current caliph further demonstrates that such phrases are not used to designate a successor.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani say about the Prophet's statement 'You are my brother and my vicegerent over my family'?
A) It is a clear nass on imamate.
B) It only refers to Ali's role over his household, not universal imamate.
C) It was said after the Prophet's death.
D) It is a forgery.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's words about Ali, however praiseworthy, do not constitute a clear text for imamate because they are limited in scope and context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that a word of praise or a delegated task from a leader or parent meant you had a broader authority than they intended? How did that assumption affect your relationship and responsibilities? What can you learn from this lesson about not reading more into words than what is actually said?
?
When have you twisted someone's words to support your own preconceived position, especially in a matter of religious belief? Are you willing to repent and commit to interpreting evidence fairly, even when it contradicts your sect or upbringing?
?
The Prophet's words to Ali were full of honor and love, yet they did not prove imamate. Are you willing to accept the truth of this argument even if it challenges a deeply held view? What is holding you back from complete submission to the evidence?

The Counter-Argument: Abu Bakr and Umar Like Harun to Moses
Baqillani counters Shi'a nass with a parallel report.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a parallel report to refute Shi'a claims of textual designation (nass) by arguing for consistency in accepting or rejecting ahad reports.

Core Idea
Consistency demands: accept both reports or reject both.

Baqillani presents a powerful logical argument against the Shi'a claim that Ali was explicitly designated as successor. He cites a report that the Prophet compared Abu Bakr and Umar to Harun with Moses. If the Shi'a accept their own ahad reports about Ali, they must accept this one too. If they reject it as ahad, then their evidence is also ahad and thus not binding. This lesson explores this dialectical refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the structure of the argument: a claim, a report, a hypothetical objection, and a counter-reply.
Pay attention to the logical flow from 'Then it is said to them' to the final conclusion.
2
Identify the two premises
The argument assumes that both sides rely on ahad reports. Find where Baqillani presents the parallel report and the challenge.
The report is: 'Abu Bakr and Umar are to me in the position of Harun to Moses.'
3
Understand the logical move
Notice that Baqillani does not prove the report's authenticity; he uses it to force consistency. If they reject it, they must reject their own proof.
This is a classic refutation by tu quoque (you too).
4
Apply the lesson
Reflect on how this argument illustrates the use of consistency as a tool in theological debate.
Consider how this principle applies to other theological disagreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : فيجب أن تثبتوا النصّ على أبي بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما بمثل هذا القول لأنه قد روى مسلم بن إبراهيم عن قزعة بن سويد عن ابن أبي مليكة عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم قال: «أبو بكـر وعمر مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى؛ فيجب النص عليهما بهذا القول. فإن قالوا : هذا أخبار الآحاد التي لا نعلمها ضرورةً ولا بدليل، قيل : إن جاز من لهم هذه الدعوى جاز لخصمكم أن يزعم أن جميع ما رويتموه وتعلقتم به في النص والتفضيل من أخبار الآحاد التي لا نعلمها ضرورة ولا بدليل فلم يلزم القول بها ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك .
Then it is said to them: You must affirm the nass on Abu Bakr and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) by similar statement, because Muslim ibn Ibrahim narrated from Qaza'a ibn Suwayd from Ibn Abi Mulayka from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Abu Bakr and Umar are to me in the position of Harun to Moses.' So the nass on them must be affirmed by this statement. If they say: 'These are ahad reports which we do not know necessarily nor by proof,' it is said: If this claim is allowed for them, then it is allowed for your opponent to claim that all that you have narrated and clung to regarding nass and tafdil are ahad reports which we do not know necessarily nor by proof, so it is not necessary to accept them, and they have no answer to that.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage is a counter-argument to the Shi'a claim of nass. The author presents a parallel report: the Prophet said Abu Bakr and Umar are to him as Harun was to Moses. If the Shi'a accept their own ahad reports about Ali, they must also accept this report about Abu Bakr and Umar, leading to the conclusion that they too were designated. But if they reject this report as ahad (isolated) and therefore not compelling, then the same objection applies to their own reports: all their evidence for nass is ahad, so it is also not compelling. This is a logical refutation: consistency demands either accepting both or rejecting both.

Key Terms
أخبار الآحاد
النص
التفضيل
الضرورة
الدليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that ahad reports are automatically rejected in Islamic theology.
Correction: Ahad reports can be accepted as evidence, but consistency requires that if one rejects a specific ahad report, one must also reject similar reports from one's own tradition.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's argument regarding the report that Abu Bakr and Umar are like Harun to Moses?
A) That report is stronger than reports about Ali.
B) The Shi'a must accept it or reject their own ahad reports.
C) It proves Abu Bakr and Umar were prophets.
D) It is a fabricated report.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Shi'a claim of nass by showing that their evidence is ahad and thus not compelling unless they accept similar reports for Abu Bakr and Umar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In religious debates, do you apply the same standard of evidence to claims you favor as to those you oppose? When have you accepted a weak argument from your own tradition while dismissing a similar argument from another? Will you commit to intellectual honesty from now on?
?
Baqillani's argument forces the opponent to either accept both reports or reject both. Think of a belief you hold that is based on a source you haven't scrutinized with the same rigor you apply to others' beliefs. What would it take for you to examine that belief honestly?
?
The Shi'a rejected the report about Abu Bakr and Umar because it was ahad, yet they accepted their own ahad reports. Have you ever shielded a cherished belief from the same criticism you level at others? What is that belief, and will you test it today with the same standard?

Refuting the 'Qadi Dayni' Analogy
Baqillani refutes the claim that 'qadi dayni' implies succession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why expressions like 'the one in charge of my debt' do not constitute an explicit designation for the imamate.

Core Idea
Mundane tasks do not imply political succession.

The Shia claim that certain phrases the Prophet used about Ali—like appointing him to settle debts—are evidence of an explicit textual nomination for immediate succession. Al-Baqillani begins his refutation by analyzing the actual meaning of such expressions. He demonstrates that they refer to specific, limited responsibilities and carry no implication of universal authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage carefully to understand the argument about the debt example.
2
Identify the key expression
Notice that the phrase 'qadi dayni' (one in charge of my debt) is being analyzed as a mere task, not a designation.
Baqillani uses an analogy with other similar expressions.
3
Understand the logical structure
See how Baqillani argues that if such phrases were taken as nass, then similar phrases would also have to apply—which they do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقاضي ديني متوجه إلى أنه أمره بقضاء دينه أو كان قد قضي عنه قبل هذا القول؛ وليس هذا من قوله أنت الإمام بعدي في شيء؛ ولهذا مالو قال خليفة الأمة في هذا الوقت زيد هذا أخي وخليفتي في أهلي وقاضي ديني لم يكن هذا عهداً إليه في الإمامة ولا من النص على ولايته في شيء، وإن كان ذلك خبراً عن فضله عنده وعظيم محله منه وأمانته وثقته؛ فلا متعلق أيضاً في هذا القول .
ثم يقال لهم : فيجب أن تثبتوا النصّ على أبي بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما بمثل هذا القول لأنه قد روى مسلم بن إبراهيم عن قزعة بن سويد عن ابن أبي مليكة عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم قال: «أبو بكـر وعمر مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى؛ فيجب النص عليهما بهذا القول. فإن قالوا : هذا أخبار الآحاد التي لا نعلمها ضرورةً ولا بدليل، قيل : إن جازت من لهم هذه الدعوى جاز لخصمكم أن يزعم أن جميع ما رويتموه وتعلقتم به في النص والتفضيل من أخبار الآحاد التي لا نعلمها ضرورة ولا بدليل فلم يلزم القول بها ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك .
ثم يقال لهم : كيف لم تعلموا أن جميع ما رويتموه ليس بنص على عليّ ولا عهداً إليه بترك علي المطالبة بذلك والاحتجاج بـه في السقيفة وعلى أهل البصرة ومعاوية وفي كل مقام كان يسوغ ذكره والاحتجاج بـه وعـدولـه إلى أن يقول بالبصرة: «بايعاني بالمدينة وخلعاني بالعراق؟ وتعلمون أن ما ظهر منه من الانقياد لأبي بكر وعمر وعثمان والأخذ لغنيمتهم ، والوطىء ، وتزويجه ابنته من عمر بن الخطاب، وإقامته حداً بحضرة عثمان، وقتاله مع أبي بكر، رضي الله عنهم أجمعين، وما ثنائه عليهما، وقوله في عمر والله ما أحد ألقى الله بصحيفته كان للحنفية من سبيهم.
And 'the one in charge of my debt' refers to him having commanded payment of his debt or having it paid before this statement; and this has nothing to do with his statement 'you are the imam after me' in any way. Therefore, if someone were to say 'the caliph of the community at this time is Zayd, this is my brother, my deputy in my family, and the one in charge of my debt,' this would not be a designation to him for the imamate nor a textual nomination for his authority in any way, even if that were an indication of his merit in his sight, his great station, his trustworthiness, and his reliability. So there is no ground for this statement either. Then it is said to them: You must then affirm the textual nomination for Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may God be pleased with them, by a similar statement because Muslim ibn Ibrahim narrated from Quza'a ibn Suwayd from Ibn Abi Mulayka from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Abu Bakr and 'Umar are to me as Aaron is to Moses'; thus textual nomination is required for them by this statement. If they say: These are single-narrator reports (akhbar al-ahad) which we do not know with certainty or by proof, it is said: If such claims are permissible for those who hold this claim, then it is permissible for your opponent to claim that all that you have narrated and adhered to concerning textual nomination and preference are single-narrator reports which we do not know with certainty or by proof, so acceptance of them becomes unnecessary, and they have no answer to that. Then it is said to them: How do you not know that all that you have narrated is not a textual nomination for 'Ali nor a designation to him, given that 'Ali refrained from demanding that and using it as an argument in the Saqifa, against the people of Basra, against Mu'awiya, and in every situation where mentioning it and arguing with it would have been appropriate, to the point that he said in Basra: 'You gave allegiance to me in Medina and deposed me in Iraq'? And you know that what appeared from him of compliance with Abu Bakr, 'Umar, and 'Uthman, his taking from their spoils, his walking, his marriage of his daughter to 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, his execution of a legal punishment in the presence of 'Uthman, his fighting alongside Abu Bakr—may God be pleased with them all—and his praise of both Abu Bakr and 'Umar, and his statement concerning 'Umar: 'By God, no one meets God with his scroll better than him'—[all this occurred] while he was one of the captives of the Banu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage is a multi-step refutation of the Shiite claim that certain expressions from the Prophet, such as 'you are to me as Aaron is to Moses' or the appointment as executor of debt, constitute an explicit textual nomination (nass) for 'Ali as the immediate successor to the Prophet. The author, al-Baqillani, structures his refutation as follows: First, he argues that the phrase 'the one in charge of my debt' (qadi dayni) refers only to the mundane task of settling debts and has no bearing on the imamate, just as calling someone 'my brother' or 'my deputy in my family' does not imply a caliphal appointment. Such phrases merely indicate closeness, trust, and merit, not a formal transfer of authority. Second, he points out that if the opponents insist on taking the 'Aaron to Moses' analogy as a nass for 'Ali, then consistency demands that they also accept a nass for Abu Bakr and 'Umar, because a hadith states that they are to the Prophet as Aaron was to Moses. Since this hadith is narrated through single chains (akhbar al-ahad) and the opponents themselves reject such reports as lacking certainty, they cannot rely on their own ahad reports for 'Ali while dismissing similar reports for Abu Bakr and 'Umar. This exposes a methodological inconsistency: if they claim certainty for their reports, they must grant certainty to the opponent's reports; if they reject ahad reports, their own position collapses. Third, al-Baqillani raises a historical argument: if there truly had been an explicit nass for 'Ali, he would have invoked it in every major confrontation—in the Saqifa after the Prophet's death, against the people of Basra during the Battle of the Camel, against Mu'awiya at Siffin, and elsewhere. Yet 'Ali never did so; instead he resorted to arguments based on general merit and community choice (e.g., 'You gave me allegiance in Medina and now you depose me in Iraq'). Moreover, 'Ali's own actions demonstrate his recognition of the legitimacy of the first three caliphs: he complied with them, participated in their military campaigns, executed punishments under 'Uthman, married his daughter to 'Umar, and praised both Abu Bakr and 'Umar. Such conduct is incompatible with believing that he was the rightful immediate successor but was unjustly usurped. Thus, the claim of an explicit nass is both logically inconsistent and historically unsubstantiated.

Key Terms
النص
العهد
الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'qadi dayni' is a designation for the caliphate.
Correction: Baqillani shows it refers to a specific task (debt repayment) and carries no implication of succession.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani, what does the phrase 'qadi dayni' actually refer to?
A) Succession to the caliphate
B) Payment of debts
C) Spiritual leadership
D) Command of the army

Key Takeaway
Expressions of trust and specific tasks do not constitute explicit textual nomination for the imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone proves reliable in a small matter, do you automatically assume they should lead every area of your life? How does this lesson force you to separate competence from authority?
?
Think of a relationship where you have given someone a specific responsibility but later felt they overstepped. Did you implicitly grant them general authority? What does Baqillani's argument say about that?
?
If the Prophet's own trust in Ali for a debt could be misread as succession, how carefully do you examine evidence before assigning unwarranted authority to others? Will you commit to distinguishing tasks from leadership from now on?

Consistency Argument with Abu Bakr and Umar
Baqillani uses a hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar to expose inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the methodological inconsistency in the Shiite use of the 'Aaron to Moses' hadith.

Core Idea
If one analogy proves nass for Ali, another proves nass for Abu Bakr and Umar.

A key argument in Sunni refutation of the Shiite nass claim is the use of the same hadith that the Shia cite. The Prophet reportedly said that Abu Bakr and Umar are to him as Aaron was to Moses. Al-Baqillani uses this to challenge the Shiite reliance on single-narrator reports (akhbar al-ahad). He shows that if they accept such reports for Ali, they must also accept them for Abu Bakr and Umar—or else reject their own evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith cited
Note the hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar being like Aaron to Moses.
2
Understand the consistency argument
Baqillani argues that if the opponents accept a similar hadith as nass for Ali, they must also accept this one for Abu Bakr and Umar.
3
Examine the objection and rebuttal
The opponents may reject the hadith as ahad. Baqillani counters that then their own ahad reports are also unacceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقاضي ديني متوجه إلى أنه أمره بقضاء دينه أو كان قد قضي عنه قبل هذا القول؛ وليس هذا من قوله أنت الإمام بعدي في شيء؛ ولهذا مالو قال خليفة الأمة في هذا الوقت زيد هذا أخي وخليفتي في أهلي وقاضي ديني لم يكن هذا عهداً إليه في الإمامة ولا من النص على ولايته في شيء، وإن كان ذلك خبراً عن فضله عنده وعظيم محله منه وأمانته وثقته؛ فلا متعلق أيضاً في هذا القول .
ثم يقال لهم : فيجب أن تثبتوا النصّ على أبي بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما بمثل هذا القول لأنه قد روى مسلم بن إبراهيم عن قزعة بن سويد عن ابن أبي مليكة عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم قال: «أبو بكـر وعمر مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى؛ فيجب النص عليهما بهذا القول. فإن قالوا : هذا أخبار الآحاد التي لا نعلمها ضرورةً ولا بدليل، قيل : إن جازت من لهم هذه الدعوى جاز لخصمكم أن يزعم أن جميع ما رويتموه وتعلقتم به في النص والتفضيل من أخبار الآحاد التي لا نعلمها ضرورة ولا بدليل فلم يلزم القول بها ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك .
ثم يقال لهم : كيف لم تعلموا أن جميع ما رويتموه ليس بنص على عليّ ولا عهداً إليه بترك علي المطالبة بذلك والاحتجاج بـه في السقيفة وعلى أهل البصرة ومعاوية وفي كل مقام كان يسوغ ذكره والاحتجاج بـه وعـدولـه إلى أن يقول بالبصرة: «بايعاني بالمدينة وخلعاني بالعراق؟ وتعلمون أن ما ظهر منه من الانقياد لأبي بكر وعمر وعثمان والأخذ لغنيمتهم ، والوطىء ، وتزويجه ابنته من عمر بن الخطاب، وإقامته حداً بحضرة عثمان، وقتاله مع أبي بكر، رضي الله عنهم أجمعين، وما ثنائه عليهما، وقوله في عمر والله ما أحد ألقى الله بصحيفته كان للحنفية من سبيهم.
And 'the one in charge of my debt' refers to him having commanded payment of his debt or having it paid before this statement; and this has nothing to do with his statement 'you are the imam after me' in any way. Therefore, if someone were to say 'the caliph of the community at this time is Zayd, this is my brother, my deputy in my family, and the one in charge of my debt,' this would not be a designation to him for the imamate nor a textual nomination for his authority in any way, even if that were an indication of his merit in his sight, his great station, his trustworthiness, and his reliability. ?

?
Baqillani shows that inconsistency in argumentation can invalidate a whole position. Examine a belief you hold: have you ever used a double standard to defend it? What would it cost you to be consistent?

Historical Argument from Ali's Conduct
Baqillani argues from Ali's history that no nass existed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ali's public conduct and failure to invoke an alleged nass undermines the claim of explicit succession.

Core Idea
Ali's actions proved he did not believe in any explicit nass.

The third and perhaps most compelling argument is historical: if Ali really believed he had been explicitly designated as successor, he would have invoked that designation when his right was contested—at the Saqifa, against the people of Basra, against Mu'awiya, and elsewhere. Yet he did not. Furthermore, his compliance with the first three caliphs, his marriage of his daughter to Umar, and his praise of Abu Bakr and Umar show that he recognized their caliphates as legitimate. Al-Baqillani uses these facts to argue that the nass claim is historically untenable.

Guided Path
1
Examine Ali's failure to invoke nass
Note the key events mentioned: Saqifa, Basra, Siffin—where Ali could have used nass but didn't.
2
Consider Ali's actions toward the first three caliphs
His compliance, marriage, and praise indicate acceptance of their caliphates.
3
Draw the conclusion
The historical evidence contradicts the claim of an explicit nass.

Source Text

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
