The Principle: Companions' Justice Cannot Be Reversed by Solitary Reports
Baqillani states the principle that proven justice cannot be overturned by ahad reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani holds that weak solitary reports cannot be used to accuse the Companions of sin, given their established justice.

Core Idea
A proven just Companion cannot be deemed sinful by weak reports.

Baqillani begins by establishing a fundamental principle: the established justice and reliability of the Companions cannot be overturned by weak solitary reports (akhbar ahad). This principle underlies his refutation of claims that Ali and Zubayr delayed their allegiance to Abu Bakr. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Baqillani links the impermissibility of attributing sin to the Companions to the weakness of the reports.
The passage begins with a statement about the Companions' concern for obedience.
2
Identify the key principle
Identify the principle that one whose faith, righteousness, and justice are established cannot be deemed sinful through solitary reports. This is the core of the argument.
Baqillani applies this principle specifically to Ali and Zubayr, but generalizes it to all Companions.
3
Understand the implication
Consider why this principle is important. It protects the reputation of the Companions from weak historical claims. Ask yourself: What types of reports would be required to accuse a Companion of sin?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
همتهم على طاعته والإذعان للحق الذي لزمهم الانقياد له . وليس يجوز لمسلم اتقى الله أن يضيف إلى علي بن أبي طالب عليه السلام والزبير بن العوام التأخر عن بيعته بأخبار آحاد واهية مجيئها من ناحية متهومة؛ لأن تأخرهم عن البيعة مع ما وصفناه من صحة وثبوتها ضرب من الإثم والعصيان وليس يمكن إضافة معصية إلى الصحابة بمثل هذا الطريق، لا سيما إذا رووا مع ذلك أن أبا بكر عليه السلام كان يدعوهم إلى الطاعة ولزوم عليهم تأخرهم ولا يسوغهم ذلك، وكذلك يجب أن ينفى عن مسعود إخراجه المُعَوِّذَتَين من المصحف ومخالفته الجماعة. وكلّ أمر روي عن الصحابة فيه تأثيم وقذف بعصيان، فيجب أن نبطله وننفيه الجماعة ويحرم عبد الله إذا ورد ورود الآحاد لأن من ثبت إيمانه وبره وعدالته لا يُفَسِّقُ بأخبار الآحاد . وعلى أن نعلم بواضح النظر كذب من ادعى تأخر علي والعباس والزبير لأن مثل هذا الخطب الجسيم في مثل هذا الأمر العظيم. يجب إشهاره وظهوره، وأن ينقل نقل مثله ؛ فكيف حفظت الأمة بأسرها وعلمت مخالفة علي لأبي بكر وغيره من الصحابة في حكم أم الولد والتوريث الذي إنما تعلمه الخاصة وذهب عنها عِلْمُ تأخره وتأخر الزبير عن البيعة حتى لا يَرِدُ إلا ورداً شاذاً ضعيفاً، وتكون الأخبار الكثيرة في معارضته ومناقضته والعادة جارية بلزوم مثل هذا للقلوب وإطلاق الألسن بذكره واشتهاره وإظهاره دون طيه وكتمانه والسهو عنه والإغفال له ؟ وإن هذا من العجب العجيب الذي لا يذهب فساده على ذي تحصيل هذا على أن حرصنا إنما هو على نفي الشين والعار وإضافة العصيان عن جلة الصحابة وعليتها بالتأخر عن بيعة قد لزمهم الانقياد لها والخنوع لصاحبها ؛ فإن أبوا ذلك ولم يقنعوا إلا بتصحيح الخلاف منهم ، قلنا لهم : فهذا إذاً من ذنوبهم، وما نرجوه أن يغفر الله لهم وحاشا للصحابة من ذلك . على أنه لا نعرف أحداً روى تأخر علي والزبير عن البيعة أياماً إلا وقد روي عنه في هذه القصة رجوعهما إلى بيعته ودخولهما في صالح ما دخل فيه المسلمون وأنهما قالا لا تثريب يا خليفة رسول الله ! ما تأخرنا عن البيعة إلا كرهنا ألا ندخل في المشورة وأنهما وصفا من فضله وسابقته وأنه صاحب الغار في كلام طويل .
Their concern was for obedience to Him and submission to the truth which they were obliged to accept. It is not permissible for a Muslim who fears Allah to attribute to Ali ibn Abi Talib (peace be upon him) and al-Zubayr ibn al-‘Awwam a delay in giving allegiance to him (Abu Bakr) based on weak solitary reports (akhbar ahad) coming from a suspect source; because their delay from the allegiance, given its correctness and establishment as we have described, would be a form of sin and disobedience, and it is not possible to attribute sin to the Companions through such a manner, especially when they also report that Abu Bakr (peace be upon him) was calling them to obedience and insisting on their delay and did not allow them that. Likewise, it is necessary to deny about Mas‘ud (Ibn Mas‘ud) his removal of the Mu‘awwidhatayn from the Mushaf and his opposition to the community. And every matter reported about the Companions that involves accusing them of sin and charging them with disobedience must be nullified and denied when it comes as solitary reports (akhbar ahad), because one whose faith, righteousness, and justice are established cannot be deemed sinful through solitary reports. Moreover, we know by clear reason the falsity of those who claim a delay of Ali, al-‘Abbas, and al-Zubayr, because such a momentous matter in such a great affair must become known and apparent, and must be transmitted in a manner befitting its magnitude. How then could the entire community have preserved and known about the opposition of Ali to Abu Bakr and other Companions regarding the ruling on the mother of a child and inheritance, which only the elite know, yet knowledge of his delay and the delay of al-Zubayr from the allegiance eluded them, so that it is only transmitted as an anomalous and weak report, while there are numerous reports contradicting and opposing it, and custom dictates that such a matter would cling to hearts and tongues would speak of it, making it famous and manifest, not concealed, hidden, and forgotten? And this is indeed a wonder whose falsity is not lost on anyone with insight. Moreover, our aim is only to remove blemish and disgrace and to absolve the leading Companions of disobedience through delay in giving allegiance which they were obliged to accept and submit to its holder. If they refuse that and are not content except to affirm their disagreement, we say to them: Then this is from their sins, and we hope that Allah will forgive them, and far be it from the Companions to do such a thing. Furthermore, we do not know anyone who narrated the delay of Ali and al-Zubayr from the allegiance for days except that he also narrated in this story their return to his allegiance and their entering into the righteous path that the Muslims entered, and that they said: 'No blame, O Caliph of the Messenger of Allah! We delayed giving allegiance only because we disliked not to enter into consultation,' and they described his virtue and precedence and that he is the Companion of the Cave, in a lengthy speech.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a refutation by Baqillani of the claim that Ali and al-Zubayr delayed giving bay'ah to Abu Bakr. He begins by stating the principle that it is not permissible for a God-fearing Muslim to attribute such a delay based on weak solitary reports (akhbar ahad) from a suspect source, because delaying bay'ah after its establishment would be a sin. He then broadens the principle: every report that accuses the Companions of sin or disobedience must be rejected when it comes as a solitary report, since one whose faith, righteousness, and justice are proven cannot be deemed sinful by such weak evidence. He gives the specific example of the claim that Ibn Mas'ud removed the Mu'awwidhatayn from the mushaf and opposed the community. Then he presents a powerful argument from general transmission: such a momentous event as the delay of Ali, al-Abbas, and al-Zubayr would have been widely known and transmitted, but instead it is only reported in a weak, anomalous manner. He contrasts this with the fact that the community preserved knowledge of Ali's differing opinion on the ruling of umm al-walad and inheritance, which was known only to the elite. The lack of widespread transmission shows the claim is false. He further notes that those who report the delay also report that Ali and al-Zubayr subsequently returned and apologized, saying they only delayed because they wanted to be part of the consultation. The passage thus refutes the allegations by both isnad criticism and a major historical argument.

Key Terms
أخبار الآحاد
عدالة
تأثيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that even weak historical reports about the Companions can be accepted if they are not about religious rulings.
Correction: Baqillani refutes this by emphasizing that the Companions' established justice makes them immune to any accusation of sin based on weak reports, regardless of the topic.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why is it not permissible to accept reports that the Companions delayed bay'ah?
A) Because such reports are from heretical sources
B) Because they are narrated via weak solitary reports contrary to the principle that proven justice cannot be overturned by such reports
C) Because all Companions were infallible
D) Because the Qur'an explicitly forbids it

Key Takeaway
Established justice of the Companions means they cannot be accused of sin based on weak solitary reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a story that questions the character of a righteous person you have known, do you apply the same standard of evidence that Baqillani applies to the Companions? What would change if you did?
?
Think of a time you formed a negative opinion about someone based on weak or secondhand information. How does this lesson challenge you to re-examine that judgment and guard your tongue?
?
The Companions' justice is established by the consensus of the Ummah. Is there anyone in your life whose good character you similarly hold as established? How can you use this principle to defend them against gossip or slander?

The Argument from General Transmission: Why the Alleged Delay Must Be False
Baqillani argues from tawatur that the alleged delay must be false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument from general transmission (tawatur) that the alleged delay of Ali and Zubayr must be false because such a momentous event would have been widely reported.

Core Idea
A major event like their alleged delay would be massively transmitted, not weakly.

Beyond the principle of justice, Baqillani deploys a powerful epistemological argument: anything as momentous as the alleged delay of leading Companions would necessarily have been transmitted widely. The fact that only weak reports exist proves the claim is false. Let's see how he builds this case.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on Baqillani's logical reasoning about what would be widely known.
He contrasts the alleged delay with other known differences among Companions.
2
Understand the tawatur argument
Recognize that Baqillani argues that a matter of this magnitude must have been transmitted via many chains (tawatur), not just weak ahad reports. The fact that it is not widely transmitted shows the claim is false.
He uses the example of Ali's known opinion on umm al-walad to highlight the point.
3
Reflect on the counter-claim
Note that Baqillani also mentions that those who report the delay also report that Ali and Zubayr later returned and apologized. This further weakens the allegation.

Source Text

What does Baqillani contrast the alleged delay of Ali and Zubayr with to show its falsehood?

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani argues that if a major event like the delay of Ali and al-Zubayr were true, it would be on everyone's lips, not just a weak report. What truth about yourself—a sin or failing—do you keep concealed, and does its concealment tell you something about its reality in your heart? Are you hiding from yourself as well as from others?
?
The lesson shows that even when someone reports the delay, they also report that Ali and al-Zubayr later apologized and recognized Abu Bakr's virtue. Do you look for the full picture when you hear a negative report about someone, especially a believer? Or do you seize on the criticism and ignore the repentance and good?
?
Baqillani hopes for forgiveness even if the delay occurred, saying 'We hope that Allah will forgive them.' Do you have such hope for believers you disagree with, or do you hold onto narratives that condemn them? How can you cultivate hope for others while still upholding truth?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
5 min
The Delay of Ali and al-Zubayr and Their Return to Bay'ah
Author refutes claims of prolonged delay by Ali and al-Zubayr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that Ali and al-Zubayr's reported delay in pledging allegiance was temporary and they ultimately accepted Abu Bakr's caliphate with apology and praise.

Core Idea
Their delay was followed by return and apology, affirming Abu Bakr's caliphate.

In debates about the early Caliphate, some claim that Ali and al-Zubayr delayed pledging allegiance to Abu Bakr, implying rejection. The author responds by noting that the very narrations that mention the delay also report their return, apology, and recognition of Abu Bakr's virtues. This passage shows that their delay was not opposition.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the English translation. Notice the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the author's main rebuttal
The author starts with 'however, we do not know anyone who narrated... except that it was also narrated...' This structure shows he is using the same narrators to prove the return.
This is a common polemical technique: using the opponent's sources against them.
3
List the three elements reported about Ali and al-Zubayr
The passage mentions their return to the pledge, their apology ('no blame...'), and their praise of Abu Bakr's virtues and his companionship in the cave. Note each.
These elements collectively demonstrate their ultimate acceptance.
4
Analyze the apology
They said they delayed only because they disliked being left out of consultation. This frames their delay as a desire for inclusion, not rejection.
The term 'caliph of the Messenger of Allah' shows they recognized Abu Bakr's authority.
5
Reflect on the broader significance
This passage defends the Sunni view of the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's caliphate by showing that even Ali and al-Zubayr accepted it.
It counters sectarian narratives that emphasize their delay as opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنه لا نعرف أحداً روى تأخر علي والزبير عن البيعة أياماً إلا وقد روي عنه في هذه القصة رجوعهما إلى بيعتة ودخولهما في صالح ما دخل فيـه المسلمون وأنهما قالا لا تثريب يا خليفة رسول الله ! ما تأخرنا عن البيعة إلا كرهنا ألا ندخل في المشورة وأنهما وصفا من فضله وسابقته وأنه صاحب الغار (۱) في كلام طويل .
However, we do not know anyone who narrated the delay of 'Ali and al-Zubayr from the pledge for days except that it was also narrated about them in this story that they returned to their pledge and entered into the good that the Muslims entered into, and that they said: 'No blame, O Caliph of the Messenger of Allah! We only delayed the pledge because we disliked to be left out of consultation,' and they described his virtue and precedence and that he was the companion of the cave (sāhib al-ghār) in lengthy speech.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage rebuts an objection concerning the delay of 'Ali and al-Zubayr in pledging allegiance to Abu Bakr. The author argues that even if there are narrations of their delay, the same sources also report that they soon returned, entered into the Muslim community, and apologized to Abu Bakr, calling him 'Caliph of the Messenger of Allah' and praising his merits, especially that he was the companion of the Prophet in the cave (al-ghār). The apology included their reason: they did not want to miss being part of the consultation (mashwara). This shows their delay was not opposition but a desire for inclusion, and they ultimately affirmed Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Key Terms
البيعة
الخليفة
الغار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the delay of 'Ali and al-Zubayr indicates they rejected Abu Bakr's caliphate.
Correction: The same narrations show that they returned, apologized, and praised Abu Bakr, proving their acceptance.

Checkpoint
What do the narrations about 'Ali and al-Zubayr also include according to the author?
A) Their criticism of Abu Bakr
B) Their return and apology
C) Their refusal to pledge
D) Their emigration to Medina

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the idea of prolonged opposition by Ali and al-Zubayr by pointing to their return, apology, and praise of Abu Bakr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disagree with a leader or an authority, do you seek to be part of the decision-making process, or do you withdraw in protest? What does this lesson teach you about the importance of staying engaged even when you are not fully satisfied?
?
The companions praised Abu Bakr's virtues even as they apologized. Think of a time you had a conflict with someone. Did you acknowledge their good qualities? How could you practice acknowledging virtues even in moments of tension?
?
Could there be a delay in your heart toward accepting a truth you already know? What might be the 'consultation' you feel you are missing, and will you take the step to return and affirm what is right?
